A. <i>sūyate, suṣuve,</i> <i>soṣyate</i> or <i>saviṣyate, asoṣṭa</i> or <i>asaviṣṭa,</i> (in Atharva-veda XIV. 1, 33. the form <i>suvāti</i> occurs, which might also be referred to rt. 1. <i>sū</i>), Inf. <i>sotum,</i> <i>savitum,</i> to beget, procreate, engender, generate; to bring forth a child, give birth to, bear, produce, yield; to confer, bestow (Ved.); to gain, acquire (Ved.); to accept, (Sāy. <i>sāviṣat = anujānātu,</i> Ṛg-veda I. 164, 26): Pass. <i>sūyate,</i> Aor. <i>asāvi,</i> to be begotten; to be brought forth: Caus. <i>sāvayati, -yitum,</i> Aor. <i>asū-</i> <i>ṣavat,</i> (according to some <i>asīṣavat</i>): Desid. of Caus. <i>suṣāvayiṣati:</i> Desid. <i>susūṣati, -te:</i> Intens. <i>soṣūyate, soṣavīti, soṣoti;</i> [cf. (thought by some to be a shortened form of <i>vasu,</i> q. v.; opposed to <i>dus,</i> q. v., and corresponding to Gr. <lang n='greek'>εὖ;</lang> in the Veda liable to become <i>ṣu,</i> see Ṛg-veda I. 36, 13, I. 112, 1, Pāṇ. VIII. 3, 107; and to lengthen a preceding vowel, see Pāṇ. VI. 3, 134; also becoming <i>sū</i> in Ṛg-veda I. 10, 11, &c.; cf. <i>sukam</i>), an enhancing particle frequently used as a prefix implying ‘good, well, excellent, excellently, beautiful, beautifully, honourable, worthy of respect or reverence, excessive, excessively, exceedingly, much, very; readily, easily, willingly, quickly’ (Ved., Sāy. <i>= suṣṭhu,</i> and in Ṛg-veda I. 112, 1, &c. used separately to qualify a verb); according to native authorities this prefix may also imply <i>anu-mati,</i> ‘assent;’ <i>sam-ṛddhi,</i> ‘prosperity;’ <i>kṛcchra,</i> ‘distress;’ [cf. Gr. <lang n='greek'>εὖ:</lang> CambroBrit. <nsi>hu, hy, he:</nsi> Armor. <nsi>he:</nsi> Hib. <nsi>so, soailce,</nsi> ‘a good fashion, good manners;’ <nsi>sucridh,</nsi> ‘easy,’ <i>= su-</i> <i>kṛta.</i>] <i>—Su-ūti, is,</i> f., Ved. good protection, kind assistance or favour. <i>—Su-kakṣa, as,</i> m., N. of the author of the hymn Ṛg-veda VIII. 81, 82 (having the patronymic Āṅgirasa). <i>—Su-kaṇṭakā,</i> f. ‘having good thorns,’ the Aloe plant, Aloe Indica. <i>—Su-</i> <i>kaṇṭha, as,</i> m., N. of a musician. <i>—Su-kaṇḍu, us,</i> m. ‘much-scratching,’ the itch. <i>—Su-kanda, as,</i> m. ‘having a good bulb,’ an onion; a yam; the esculent root Arum Campanulatum; a sort of grass, Scirpus Kysoor; other bulbous plants <i>(= vārāhī-kanda; =</i> <i>dharaṇī-kanda)</i>. <i>—Su-kandaka, as,</i> m. an onion. <i>—Su-kandin, ī,</i> m. Arum Campanulatum. <i>—Su-</i> <i>kanyaka</i> or <i>su-kanyāka, as, ā, am,</i> having a beautiful maiden, (Vopa-deva VII. 23.) <i>—Su-kanyā,</i> f. a beautiful girl; N. of a daughter of Śaryāti (and wife of the Ṛṣi Cyavana). <i>—Su-kaparda, as, ā,</i> <i>am,</i> having beautiful braided hair. <i>—Su-kara, as, ā,</i> or <i>ī, am,</i> easy to be done, practicable, feasible, attainable; easy to be managed, doing well; (<i>ā</i>), f. a tractable cow; (<i>am</i>), n. doing good, charity, benevolence. <i>—Sukara-sandhi, is, is, i,</i> easily joined or united. <i>—Su-karṇaka, as, ikā, am,</i> having beautiful ears; (<i>as</i>), m. a particular tree, <i>= hasti-</i> <i>kanda; (ikā),</i> f. the plant Salvinia Cucullata. <i>—Su-</i> <i>karṇī,</i> f. the colocynth. <i>—Su-karma, ās,</i> m. pl., N. of a class of deities. <i>—Su-karman, ā, ā, a,</i> one whose deeds are righteous or virtuous, performing good works;
